Show that\nhypotenuse AC = 2 BC.\nSolution: Produce CB to a point D such that BC = BD\nand join AD.\nIn ∆ ABC and ∆ ABD, we have\nBC = BD\n(By construction)\nAB = AB\n(Same side)\n∠ABC = ∠ABD\n(Each of 90°)\nTherefore,\n∆ ABC ≅∆ ABD\n(SAS)\nSo,\n∠CAB = ∠DAB\n(1)\nand\nAC = AD\n(2)\nThus,\n∠CAD = ∠CAB + ∠BAD = x + x = 2x   [From (1)]\n(3)\nand\n∠ACD = ∠ADB = 2x\n[From (2), AC = AD]\n(4)\nThat is, ∆ ACD is an equilateral triangle. [From (3) and (4)]\nor\nAC = CD, i.e.,  AC = 2 BC  (Since BC = BD)\nSample Question 2 : Prove that if in two triangles two angles and the included side of\none triangle are equal to two angles and the included side of the other triangle, then the\ntwo triangles are congruent.\nSolution: See proof of Theorem 7.1 of Class IX Mathematics\nTextbook.\nSample Question 3 : If the bisector of an angle of a triangle\nalso bisects the opposite side, prove that the triangle is isosceles.\nSolution : We are given a point D on side BC of a ∆ ABC such\nthat ∠BAD = ∠CAD and BD = CD (see Fig. 7.10).
